personnel) only counted once.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Bayonne</b> (<small>French pronunciation:&#160;&#8203;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[baj\xc9\x94n]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Gascon_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Gascon dialect">Gascon</a>: <i>Baiona</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Occitan" title="Help:IPA/Occitan">[ba\xcb\x88jun\xc9\x94]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>: <i lang="eu">Baiona</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Basque" title="Help:IPA/Basque">[baiona]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Bayona</i>) is a city and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">commune</a> and one of the two <a href="/wiki/Subprefectures_in_France" title="Subprefectures in France">sub-prefectures</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">department</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Nouvelle-Aquitaine" title="Nouvelle-Aquitaine">Nouvelle-Aquitaine</a> region of south-western France.<sup id="cite_ref-Lion_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lion-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is located at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Nive" title="Nive">Nive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a> rivers in the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural region">cultural region</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a>, as well as the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a> where the Aquitaine basin joins the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pyrenees" title="Pre-Pyrenees">Pre-Pyrenees</a>.\n</p><p>Together with nearby <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Luz" title="Saint-Jean-de-Luz">Saint-Jean-de-Luz</a>, and several smaller communes, Bayonne forms an urban area with 288,359 inhabitants at the 2012 census,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> 45,855 of whom lived in the city of Bayonne proper.<sup id="cite_ref-INSEE_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INSEE-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The site on the left bank of the Nive and the Adour was probably occupied before <a href="/wiki/Ancient_times" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient times">ancient times</a> as a fortified enclosure was attested in the 1st century at the time when the <a href="/wiki/Tarbelli" title="Tarbelli">Tarbelli</a> occupied the territory. Archaeological studies have confirmed the presence of a Roman <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">castrum</a>, a stronghold in <a href="/wiki/Novempopulania" title="Novempopulania">Novempopulania</a> at the end of the 4th century before the city was populated by the <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a>.\n</p><p>In 1023 Bayonne was the capital of <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a> and, in the 12th century, extended to and beyond the Nive. At that time the first bridge was built over the Adour. The city came under the domination of the English in 1152 through the marriage of <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Aquitaine" title="Eleanor of Aquitaine">Eleanor of Aquitaine</a>: it became militarily and, above all, commercially important thanks to maritime trade. It was separated from the Viscount of Labourd in 1177 by <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard the Lion Heart</a>. In 1451 the city was taken by the Crown of France after the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years&#39; War">Hundred Years\' War</a>. The loss of trade with the English and the silting up of the river as well as the movement of the city towards the north weakened it. The district of Saint-Esprit developed anyway thanks to the arrival of a Jewish population fleeing the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>. From this community Bayonne gained its reputation for chocolate. The course of the Adour was changed in 1578 under the direction of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Louis_de_Foix&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Louis de Foix (page does not exist)">Louis de Foix</a> and the river returned to its former mouth, returning business lost to Bayonne for over a hundred years. In the 17th century the city was fortified by <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Le_Prestre_de_Vauban" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Le Prestre de Vauban">Vauban</a>. In 1814 Bayonne and its surroundings were the scene of fighting between the Napoleonic troops and the Spanish-Anglo-Portuguese coalition led by the <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Duke of Wellington</a>: the city then underwent its final <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bayonne" title="Battle of Bayonne">siege</a>.\n</p><p>In 1951 the Lacq gas field was discovered whose extracted <a href="/wiki/Sulphur" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulphur">sulphur</a> and associated oil are shipped from the port of Bayonne. During the second half of the 20th century many housing estates were built forming new districts on the periphery and the city was extended to form a conurbation with <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>: this agglomeration became the heart of a vast Basque-Landes urban area.\n</p><p>Bayonne was, in 2014, a commune with over 45,000 inhabitants, the heart of the urban area of Bayonne and of the <i>Agglomeration C\xc3\xb4te Basque-Adour</i> which includes <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>. It is an important part of the Basque <i>Bayonne-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Eurocity</i> and it plays the role of economic capital of the Adour basin. Modern industry\xe2\x80\x94metallurgy and chemicals\xe2\x80\x94are established to take advantage of procurement opportunities and sea shipments through the harbour. It is now mostly business services which today represent the largest source of employment. Bayonne is also a cultural capital, a city with strong Basque and Gascon influences and a rich historical past. Its heritage lies in its architecture, the diversity of collections in museums, its gastronomic specialties, and traditional events such as the famous <a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAtes_de_Bayonne" title="F\xc3\xaates de Bayonne">F\xc3\xaates de Bayonne</a>.\n</p><p>The inhabitants of the commune are known as <i>Bayonnais</i> or <i>Bayonnaises</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div shops</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#Workshops_and_Industry"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Workshops and Industry</span></a></li>\n<li href="#The_port_of_Bayonne"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">The port of Bayonne</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-50"><a href="#Tourism_services"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Tourism services</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#Sights"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Sights</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#Personalities"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Personalities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#In_popular_culture"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">In popular culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-54"><a href="#Notes_and_references"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Notes and references</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-55"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-56"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-57"><a href="#Insee"><span class="tocnumber">11.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Insee</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-58"><a href="#Bibliographic_sources"><span class="tocnumber">11.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliographic sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-59"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11.3</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Bayonne is located in the south-west of France on the western border between <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">Basque Country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a>. It developed at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a> and tributary on the left bank, the <a href="/wiki/Nive" title="Nive">Nive</a>, 6&#160;km from the Atlantic coast. The commune was part of the Basque province of <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a>.\n</p>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Neighbouring_communes_and_villages" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div id="Neighbouring_communes_and_villages" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><b>Neighbouring communes and villages</b><sup id="cite_ref-Google_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Google-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin:0; text-align:center;"><tbody><tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boucau" title="Boucau">Boucau</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Tamos" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamos">Tamos</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Saint-Martin-de-Seignanx" title="Saint-Martin-de-Seignanx">Saint-Martin-de-Seignanx</a></td>\n</tr><tr>\n<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a></td>\n<td style="width:33%;">\n<div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/14px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png" title="North" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/21px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pfeil_oben.svg/28px-Pfeil_oben.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="595" /></div>\n<div style="white-space:nowrap;"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/17px-Pfeil_links.svg.png" title="West" width="17" height="14" style="vertical-align: middle" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/25px-Pfeil_links.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pfeil_links.svg/33px-Pfeil_links.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="501" /><b style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:middle; margin:0.75em 1em">Bayonne</b><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/17px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png" title="East" width="17" height="14" style="vertical-align: middle" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/25px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Pfeil_rechts.svg/33px-Pfeil_rechts.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="501" /></div>\n<div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/14px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png" title="South" width="14" height="17" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/21px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Pfeil_unten.svg/28px-Pfeil_unten.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="501" data-file-height="595" /></div>\n</td>\n<td style="width:33%"><a href="/wiki/Saint-Barth%C3%A9lemy,_Landes" title="Saint-Barth\xc3\xa9lemy, Landes">Saint-Barth\xc3\xa9lemy</a></td>\n</tr><tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Bassussarry" title="Bassussarry">Bassussarry</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Villefranque,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Villefranque, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Villefranque</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Lahonce" title="Lahonce">Lahonce</a></td>\n</tr></tbody></table></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_relief">Geology and relief</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology and relief">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne occupies a territory characterized by a flat relief to the west and to the north towards the <a href="/wiki/Landes_forest" title="Landes forest">Landes forest</a>, tending to slightly raise towards the south and east. The city has developed at the confluence of the Adour and Nive 6 kilometres (3.7 miles) from the ocean. The meeting point of the two rivers coincides with a narrowing of the Adour valley. Above this the alluvial plain extends for nearly thirty kilometres (19 miles) towards both <a href="/wiki/Tercis-les-Bains" title="Tercis-les-Bains">Tercis-les-Bains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peyrehorade" title="Peyrehorade">Peyrehorade</a>, and is characterized by swampy meadows called <i>barthes</i> which are influenced by floods and high tides.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> Downstream from this point the river has shaped a large bed in the sand dunes creating a significant bottleneck at the confluence.\n</p><p>The occupation of the hill that dominates this narrowing of the valley developed through a gradual spread across the lowlands by building embankments and the <a href="/wiki/Aggradation" title="Aggradation">aggradation</a> from flood soil.<sup id="cite_ref-p4_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p4-7">&#91;PH 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Nive has played a leading role in the development of the Bayonne river system in recent geological time by the formation of alluvial terraces that form the sub-soil of Bayonne beneath the surface accumulations of silt and aeolian sands.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-8">&#91;PH 2&#93;</a></sup> The drainage network of the western <a href="/wiki/Pre-Pyrenees" title="Pre-Pyrenees">Pre-Pyrenees</a> evolved mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary" title="Quaternary">Quaternary</a> from south-east to northwest oriented east-west. The Adour was then captured by the gaves and this system, together with the Nive, led to the emergence of a new alignment of the lower Adour and the Adour-Nive confluence. This capture has been dated to the early Quaternary (80,000 years ago).<sup id="cite_ref-p3_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-8">&#91;PH 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before this capture the Nive had deposited pebbles from the <a href="/wiki/Mindel_glaciation" title="Mindel glaciation">Mindel glaciation</a> of medium to large sizes that slowed erosion of the hills causing the bottleneck at Bayonne. After the deposit of the lowest alluvial terrace (10&#160;to 15 metres (33\xe2\x80\x9349 feet) high at Grand Bayonne), the course of the Adour became fixed in its lower reaches.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-8">&#91;PH 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Subsequent to these deposits there was a rise in sea level in the <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> period (from 15,000 to 5000 years ago) which explains the invasion of the lower valleys with fine sand, peat, and mud with a thickness of more than 40 metres (130 feet) below the current bed of the Adour and the Nive in Bayonne. These same deposits are spread across the barthes.<sup id="cite_ref-p4_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p4-7">&#91;PH 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the late Quaternary the topographic physiognomy we know today was formed\xe2\x80\x94i.e. a set of hills overlooking a swampy lowland. The promontory of <a href="/wiki/Bassussarry" title="Bassussarry">Bassussarry</a>\xe2\x80\x93Marracq ultimately extended to the labourdin foothills, dying out at the Grand Bayonne hill is an example. Similarly, on the right bank of the Nive, the heights of Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Neuf (Mocoron Hill) met the latest advance of the plateau of Saint-Pierre-d\'Irube (height 30&#160;to 35 metres (98\xe2\x80\x93115 feet)).<sup id="cite_ref-p4_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p4-7">&#91;PH 1&#93;</a></sup> On the right bank of the Adour the heights of Castelnau (today the citadel) with an altitude of 35&#160;to 40 metres (115\xe2\x80\x93131 feet), and Fort (today Saint-Esprit) with an altitude of 20&#160;to 25 metres (66\xe2\x80\x9382 feet) rise above the Barthes of the Adour, the Nive, Bourgneuf, Saint-Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric, Sainte-Croix, Aritxague, and Pontots.<sup id="cite_ref-p4_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p4-7">&#91;PH 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The area of the commune is 2,168 hectares (5,360 acres) and its altitude varies between 0&#160;to 55 metres (0\xe2\x80\x93180 feet).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hydrography">Hydrography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hydrography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg/330px-Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Adour_HdV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nive" title="Nive">Nive</a> from the right bank of the Adour.</div></div></div>\n<p>The city is traversed by the Adour.<sup id="cite_ref-sandre_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandre-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The river is part of the <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a> network from its source at <a href="/wiki/Bagn%C3%A8res-de-Bigorre" title="Bagn\xc3\xa8res-de-Bigorre">Bagn\xc3\xa8res-de-Bigorre</a> to its exit to the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> after Bayonne, between <a href="/wiki/Tarnos" title="Tarnos">Tarnos</a> (Landes) for the right bank and <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a> (Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques) for the left bank.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apart from the <a href="/wiki/Nive" title="Nive">Nive</a>, which converges on the left bank of the Adour after 79.3 kilometres (49.3 miles) of a sometimes tumultuous course, two tributaries join the Adour in Bayonne commune: the <i>Ruisseau de Portou</i> and the <i>Ruisseau du Moulin Esbouc</i>. Tributaries of the Nive are the <i>Ruisseau de Hillans</i> and the <i>Ruisseau d\'Urdaintz</i> which both rise in the commune.<sup id="cite_ref-Geo_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geo-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The nearest weather station is that of Biarritz-Anglet.\n</p><p>The climate of Bayonne is relatively similar to that of its neighbour Biarritz, described below, with fairly heavy rainfall; The oceanic climate is due to the proximity of the Atlantic Ocean. The average winter temperature is around 8&#160;\xc2\xb0C and is around 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C in summer. The lowest temperature recorded was \xe2\x88\x9212.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C on 16 January 1985 and the highest 40.6&#160;\xc2\xb0C on 4 August 2003. Rains on the Basque coast are rarely persistent except during winter storms. They often take the form of intense thunderstorms of short duration.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable centre" style="text-align:right">\n<caption class="hidden">Comparison of local Meteorological data color:#000000;">192.8\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C0C024; color:#000000;">141.7\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B0B082; color:#000000;">103.8\n</td>\n<td style="background: #A1A1A1; color:#000000;">88.3\n</td>\n<td style="background: #C8C800; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">1,887.3\n</td></tr>\n\n\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source &#35;1: M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o France<sup id="cite_ref-M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MFclimat2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFclimat2-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;">Source &#35;2: Infoclimat.fr (humidity and snowy days, 1961\xe2\x80\x931990)<sup id="cite_ref-Infoclimat_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Infoclimat-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communication_and_transport">Communication and transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Communication and transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png/220px-Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png/330px-Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png/440px-Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Transport_interurbain_autour_de_Bayonne_03092014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Public transport around Bayonne: railway lines are black, the intercity bus lines Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques are green and those of Landes purple. The PTU (perimeter of urban transport, which operates the Chronoplus network is uncharted here) is bounded by a red line.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_(2).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png/220px-Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png/330px-Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png/440px-Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_%282%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1068" data-file-height="1132" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_-_Voies_de_communication_(2).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Means of transport (water, roads, bridges, and railways).</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road_communications">Road communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Road communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne is located at the intersection of the <a href="/wiki/A63_autoroute" title="A63 autoroute">A63 autoroute</a> (Bordeaux-Spain) and the D1 extension of the <a href="/wiki/A64_autoroute" title="A64 autoroute">A64 autoroute</a> (towards <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>). The city is served by three interchanges\xe2\x80\x94two of them on the A63: exit <a href="/wiki/File:Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Sinnbild Autobahnausfahrt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/15px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png" width="15" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/23px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/30px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="347" /></a>&#160;6&#160;<b></b> (Bayonne Nord) serves the northern districts of Bayonne but also allows quick access to the centre while exit <a href="/wiki/File:Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Sinnbild Autobahnausfahrt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/15px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png" width="15" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/23px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/30px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="347" /></a>&#160;5&#160;<b></b> (Bayonne Sud) provides access to the south and also serves <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>. The third exit is the D1 / A64 via the Mousserolles interchange (exit <a href="/wiki/File:Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg" class="image"><img alt="Sinnbild Autobahnausfahrt.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/15px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png" width="15" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/23px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg/30px-Sinnbild_Autobahnausfahrt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="486" data-file-height="347" /></a>&#160;1&#160;<b></b> Bayonne Mousserolles) which links the district of the same name and also serves the neighbouring communes of <a href="/wiki/Mouguerre" title="Mouguerre">Mouguerre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre-d%27Irube" title="Saint-Pierre-d&#39;Irube">Saint-Pierre-d\'Irube</a>.\n</p><p>Bayonne was traversed by <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale_10" title="Route nationale 10">Route nationale 10</a> connecting <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hendaye" title="Hendaye">Hendaye</a> but this is now downgraded to a departmental road D810. <a href="/wiki/Route_nationale" title="Route nationale">Route nationale</a> 117, linking Bayonne to Toulouse has been downgraded to departmental road D817.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridges">Bridges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Bridges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Adour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bayonne_Adour.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Adour.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bayonne_Adour.jpg/330px-Bayonne_Adour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Bayonne_Adour.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Adour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Adour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Saint-Esprit bridge over the <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>There are several bridges over both the Nive and the Adour linking the various districts.\n</p><p>Coming from upstream on the Adour there is the A63 bridge, then the Saint-Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric bridge which carries the D 810, then the railway bridge that replaced the old Eiffel iron bridge, the Saint-Esprit bridge, and finally the Grenet bridge. The Saint-Esprit bridge connects the Saint-Esprit district to the Amiral-Bergeret dock just upstream of the confluence with the river Nive. In 1845 the old bridge, originally made&#160;??of wood, was rebuilt in masonry with seven arches supporting a deck 230 metres (750 feet) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-p118_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p118-20">&#91;FL 1&#93;</a></sup> It was then called the Nemours Bridge in honour of <a href="/wiki/Prince_Louis,_Duke_of_Nemours" title="Prince Louis, Duke of Nemours">Louis of Orleans</a>, sixth Duke of Nemours, who laid the first stone. The bridge was finally called Saint-Esprit. Until 1868 the bridge had a moving span near the left bank. It was expanded in 1912 to facilitate the movement of horse-drawn <a href="/wiki/Carriage" title="Carriage">carriages</a> and motor vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-p118_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p118-20">&#91;FL 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On the Nive coming from upstream to downstream there is the A63 bridge then the <i>Pont Blanc</i> (White bridge)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;Note 2&#93;</a></sup> railway bridge, and then D810 bridge, the G\xc3\xa9nie bridge (or <i>Pont Millitaire</i>), the Pannecau bridge, the Marengo bridge<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;Note 3&#93;</a></sup> leading to the covered markets, and the Mayou Bridge<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;Note 4&#93;</a></sup> The Pannecau bridge was long named <i>Bertaco bridge</i> and was rebuilt in masonry under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p25_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p25-24">&#91;FL 2&#93;</a></sup> According to Fran\xc3\xa7ois Lafitte Houssat, "[...] a municipal ordinance of 1327 provided for the imprisonment of any quarrellsome woman of bad character in an iron cage dropped into the waters of the Nive River from the bridge. The practice lasted until 1780 [...]"<sup id="cite_ref-p25_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p25-24">&#91;FL 2&#93;</a></sup> This punishment bore the evocative name of <i>cubainhade</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-p20_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p20-25">&#91;DN 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling_network">Cycling network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cycling network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The commune is traversed by the <i><a href="/wiki/EV1_The_Atlantic_Coast_Route" title="EV1 The Atlantic Coast Route">V\xc3\xa9lodyss\xc3\xa9e</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure" title="Cycling infrastructure">Bicycle paths</a> are located along the left bank of the Adour, a large part of the left bank of the Nive, and along various axes of the city where there are some bicycle lanes. The city offers free bicycles on loan.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">Public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_network">Urban network</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Urban network">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Most of the lines of the <i>Chronoplus</i> bus network operated by the <i>Transdev agglomeration of Bayonne</i> link Bayonne to other communes in the urban transport perimeter: <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bidart" title="Bidart">Bidart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boucau" title="Boucau">Boucau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre-d%27Irube" title="Saint-Pierre-d&#39;Irube">Saint-Pierre-d\'Irube</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarnos" title="Tarnos">Tarnos</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;Note 5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The Bayonne free shuttle Bayonne serves the city centre (Grand and Petit Bayonne) by connecting several parking stations; other free shuttles perform other short trips within the commune.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Interurban_networks">Interurban networks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Interurban networks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Bayonne is connected to many cities in the western half of the department such as <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Luz" title="Saint-Jean-de-Luz">Saint-Jean-de-Luz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Palais,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Saint-Palais, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Saint-Palais</a> by the Pyrenees-Atlantiques long distance coach network of <i>Transport 64</i> managed by the General Council. Since the network restructuring in the summer of 2013, the lines converge on Bayonne.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Bayonne is also served by services from the <a href="/wiki/Landes_(department)" title="Landes (department)">Landes</a> departmental network, <i>XL\'R</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Bayonne" title="Gare de Bayonne">Gare de Bayonne</a> is located in the Saint-Esprit district and is an important station on the <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux-Irun_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Bordeaux-Irun railway">Bordeaux-Irun railway</a>. It is also the terminus of lines leading from <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> to Bayonne and from Bayonne to <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port" title="Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port">Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port</a>. It is served by <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s" title="Intercit\xc3\xa9s">Intercit\xc3\xa9s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lun%C3%A9a" class="mw-redirect" title="Lun\xc3\xa9a">Lun\xc3\xa9a</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TER_Aquitaine" title="TER Aquitaine">TER Aquitaine</a> trains (to <a href="/wiki/Hendaye" title="Hendaye">Hendaye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port" title="Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port">Saint-Jean-Pied-de-Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dax,_Landes" title="Dax, Landes">Dax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pau,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Pau, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Pau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tarbes" title="Tarbes">Tarbes</a>).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transport">Air transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Air transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Bayonne is served by the <a href="/wiki/Biarritz_%E2%80%93_Anglet_%E2%80%93_Bayonne_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Biarritz \xe2\x80\x93 Anglet \xe2\x80\x93 Bayonne Airport">Biarritz \xe2\x80\x93 Anglet \xe2\x80\x93 Bayonne Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_code" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA code">IATA code</a>: BIQ \xe2\x80\xa2 <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO code</a>: LFBZ), located on the communal territories of Anglet and Biarritz.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;Note 6&#93;</a></sup> The airport was returned to service in 1954 after repair of damage from bombing during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>.\n</p><p>Airport management is carried out by the joint association for the development and operation of the airport of Biarritz-Anglet-Bayonne, which includes the Chamber of Commerce and Industry of Bayonne Basque Country, the agglomeration of C\xc3\xb4te Basque-Adour, the departments of Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques and Landes, and the commune of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Luz" title="Saint-Jean-de-Luz">Saint-Jean-de-Luz</a>. The airport of Biarritz-Anglet-Bayonne had nearly 1.1 million passengers in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It has regular connections to <a href="/wiki/Paris-Orly" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Orly">Paris-Orly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris-CDG" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-CDG">Paris-CDG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nice" title="Nice">Nice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted" class="mw-redirect" title="London Stansted">London Stansted</a> and from March to October 2014 had connections with: <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_de_Marseille_Provence" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xa9roport de Marseille Provence">Marseille</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=A%C3%A9roport_de_Strasbourg-Entzheim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="A\xc3\xa9roport de Strasbourg-Entzheim (page does not exist)">Strasbourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9roport_de_Lille-Lesquin" class="mw-redirect" title="A\xc3\xa9roport de Lille-Lesquin">Lille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels_South_Charleroi_Airport" title="Brussels South Charleroi Airport">Brussels South Charleroi Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Skavsta_Airport" title="Stockholm Skavsta Airport">Stockholm-Skavsta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Arlanda_Airport" title="Stockholm Arlanda Airport">Stockholm-Arlanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London-Gatwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Airport" title="Copenhagen Airport">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Airport,_Gardermoen" title="Oslo Airport, Gardermoen">Oslo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Airport" title="Helsinki Airport">Helsinki</a>. Airline companies serving the airport at 1 November 2014 were: <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Regional" class="mw-redirect" title="Etihad Regional">Etihad Regional</a>, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hop!" class="mw-redirect" title="Hop!">Hop!</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">SAS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twin_Jet" title="Twin Jet">Twin Jet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volotea" title="Volotea">Volotea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>While the modern <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> spelling is <i>Baiona</i> and the same in <a href="/wiki/Gascon_language" title="Gascon language">Gascon</a> <a href="/wiki/Occitan" class="mw-redirect" title="Occitan">Occitan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Toponimia_(leku-izenak)_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toponimia_(leku-izenak)-34">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> "the name <i>Bayonne</i> poses a number of problems both historical and linguistic which have still not been clarified".<sup id="cite_ref-Iglesias_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iglesias-35">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> There are different interpretations of its meaning.\n</p><p>The termination <i>-onne</i> in <i>Bayonne</i> can come from many in hydronyms <i>-onne</i> or toponyms derived from that. In certain cases the element <i>-onne</i> follows an Indo-European theme: <i>*ud-r/n</i> (Greek <i>h\xc3\xbad\xc5\x8dr</i> giving hydro, <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic</a> <i>watt</i> meaning "water") hence <i>*udn\xc4\x81</i> meaning "water" giving <i>unna</i> then <i>onno</i> in the glossary of <a href="/wiki/Vienne" title="Vienne">Vienne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <i>Unna</i> therefore would refer to the Adour. This toponymic type evoking a river traversing a locality is common. The appellative <i>unna</i> seems to be found in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a> (<i>Garunna</i> 1st century; <i>Garonna</i> 4th century). However it is possible to see a pre-Celtic suffix <i>-ona</i> in the name of the <a href="/wiki/Charente_(river)" title="Charente (river)">Charente</a> (<i>Karantona</i> in 875) or the <a href="/wiki/Charentonne" title="Charentonne">Charentonne</a> (<i>Carentona</i> in 1050).<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It could also be an augmentative <a href="/wiki/Gascon_language" title="Gascon language">Gascon</a> from the original <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> radical <i>Baia-</i> with the suffix <i>-ona\' in the sense of "vast expanse of water" or a name derived from the Basque </i>bai<i> meaning "river" and </i>ona<i> meaning "good", hence "good river".</i>\n</p><p>The proposal by Eugene Goyheneche repeated by Manex Goyhenetche and supported by Jean-Baptiste Orpustan is <i>bai una</i>, "the place of the river" or <i>bai ona</i> "hill by the river"\xe2\x80\x94<i>Ibai</i> means "river" in Basque and <i>muinoa</i> means "hill".\n</p><p>"It has perhaps been lost from sight that many urban place names in France, from north to south, came from the element <i>Bay-</i> or <i>Bayon-</i> such as: <a href="/wiki/Bayons" title="Bayons">Bayons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayonville" title="Bayonville">Bayonville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayonvillers" title="Bayonvillers">Bayonvillers</a> and pose the unusual problem of whether they are Basque or Gascon"\n</p><p>adds Pierre Hourmat.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-38">&#91;PiH 1&#93;</a></sup> However, the most ancient form of Bayonne: <i>Baiona</i>, clearly indicates a feminine or a theme of <i>-a</i> whereas this is not the case for B\xc3\xa9on or Bayon. In addition, the <i>Bayon-</i> in Bayonville or Bayonvillers in northern France is clearly the personal Germanic name <i>Baio</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_attestations">Old attestations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Old attestations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The names of the Basque province of <a href="/wiki/Labourd" title="Labourd">Labourd</a> and the locality of Bayonne have been attested from an early period with the place name <i>Bayonne</i> appearing in the Latin form <i>Lapurdum</i> after a period during which the two names could in turn designate a Viscounty or Bishopric.<sup id="cite_ref-Orpustan_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orpustan-40">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Labourd</i> and <i>Bayonne</i> were synonymous and used interchangeably until the 12th century before being differentiated: Labord for the province and Bayonne for the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Orpustan_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orpustan-40">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The attribution of Bayonne as <i>Civitas Boatium</i>, a place mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Antonine_Itinerary" title="Antonine Itinerary">Antonine Itinerary</a> and by Paul Raymond in his 1863 dictionary, has been abandoned. The city of the <i>Bo\xc3\xafates</i> may possibly be <a href="/wiki/La_Teste-de-Buch" title="La Teste-de-Buch">La Teste-de-Buch</a> but is certainly not Bayonne.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;Note 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The following table details the origins of Labord, Bayonne, and other names in the commune.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name</th>\n<th>Spelling</th>\n<th>Date</th>\n<th>Source</th>\n<th>Page</th>\n<th>Origin</th>\n<th>Description\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Bayonne</b></td>\n<td>Tribunus href="/wiki/Paul_Raymond_(archivist)" title="Paul Raymond (archivist)">Raymond</a>:</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" numbers indicated in the table. <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Raymond_42-0" class="reference"><a
