href="#cite_note-Camara-48">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the absence of accurate objective data there is some credence to the probable existence of a fishing village on the site in a period prior to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_times" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient times">ancient times</a>. Numerous traces of human occupation have been found in the Bayonne region from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> especially in the discoveries at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre-d%27Irube" title="Saint-Pierre-d&#39;Irube">Saint-Pierre-d\'Irube</a>, a neighbouring locality.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;Note 8&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, the presence of a mound about 14 metres (46 feet) high has been detected in the current Cathedral Quarter overlooking the Nive which formed a natural protection and a usable port on the left bank of the Nive. At the time the mound was surrounded north and west by the Adour swamps. At its foot lies the famous "Bayonne Sea"\xe2\x80\x94the junction of the two rivers\xe2\x80\x94which may have been about 1,200 metres (3,900 feet) wide between Saint-Esprit and the Grand Bayonne and totally covered the current location of Bourg-Neuf (in the district of Petit Bayonne). To the south the last bend of the Nive widens near the Saint-L\xc3\xa9on hills.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-51">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, the narrowing of the Adour valley allows easier crossing than anywhere else along the entire length of the estuary.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In conclusion, the strategic importance of this height was so obvious it must be presumed that it has always been inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-51">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_times">Ancient times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ancient times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg/220px-Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg.png" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg/330px-Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg/440px-Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="878" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aquitani_tribes_map-fr.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of <a href="/wiki/Novempopulania" title="Novempopulania">Novempopulania</a> indicating the position of the <a href="/wiki/Tarbelli" title="Tarbelli">Tarbelli</a> territory north-west of the Pyrenees.</div></div></div>\n<p>The oldest documented human occupation site is located on a hill overlooking the Nive and its confluence with the Adour.<sup id="cite_ref-p3_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p3-38">&#91;PiH 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 1st century AD, during the Roman occupation, Bayonne already seems to have been of some importance since the Romans surrounded the city with a wall to keep out the <a href="/wiki/Tarbelli" title="Tarbelli">Tarbelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquitani" title="Aquitani">Aquitani</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Basque" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Basque">proto-Basque</a> who then occupied a territory that extended south of modern-day <a href="/wiki/Landes_(department)" title="Landes (department)">Landes</a>, to the modern French Basque country, the <a href="/wiki/Chalosse" title="Chalosse">Chalosse</a>, the valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a>, the mountain streams of <a href="/wiki/Pau,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Pau, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Pau, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques</a>, and to the <a href="/wiki/Gave_d%27Oloron" title="Gave d&#39;Oloron">Gave d\'Oloron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The archaeological discoveries of October and November 1995 provided a shred of evidence to support this projection. In the four layers of sub-soil along the foundation of the Gothic cathedral (in the "apse of the cathedral" area) a 2-metre depth was found of old objects from the end of the 1st century\xe2\x80\x94in particular sigillated Gallic ceramics from <a href="/wiki/Montans" title="Montans">Montans</a> imitating Italian styles, thin-walled bowls, and fragments of <a href="/wiki/Amphorae" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphorae">amphorae</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;Note 9&#93;</a></sup> In the "southern sector" near the cloister door there were objects from the second half of the 1st century as well as coins from the first half of the 3rd century.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A very high probability of human presence, not solely military, seems to provisionally confirm the occupation of the site at least around the 3rd century.\n</p><p>A Roman <a href="/wiki/Castra" title="Castra">castrum</a> dating to the end of the 4th century has been proven as a fortified place of <a href="/wiki/Novempopulania" title="Novempopulania">Novempopulania</a>. Named <i>Lapurdum</i>, the name became the name of the province of <i>Labourd</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;Note 10&#93;</a></sup> According to Eugene Goyheneche the name <i>Baiona</i> designated the city, the port, and the cathedral while that of <i>Lapurdum</i> was only a territorial designation.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This Roman settlement was strategic as it allowed the monitoring of the trans-Pyrenean roads and of local people rebellious to the Roman power. The construction covered 6 to 10 hectares according to several authors.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;Note 11&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;Note 12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The geographical location of the locality at the crossroads of a river system oriented from east to west and the road network connecting Europe to the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> from north to south predisposed the site to the double role of fortress and port.<sup id="cite_ref-p149_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p149-61">&#91;EG 1&#93;</a></sup> The city, after being Roman, alternated between the <a href="/wiki/Vascones" title="Vascones">Vascones</a> and the English for three centuries from the 12th to the 15th century.\n</p><p>The Romans left the city in the 4th century and the Basques, who had always been present, dominated the former Novempopulania province between the <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a>, the Ocean, and the Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es. Novempopulania was renamed <a href="/wiki/Vasconia" class="mw-redirect" title="Vasconia">Vasconia</a> and then Gascony after a Germanic deformation (resulting from the <a href="/wiki/Visigoth" class="mw-redirect" title="Visigoth">Visigoth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> invasions). Basquisation of the plains region was too weak against the advance of romanization. From the mixture between the Basque and Latin language <a href="/wiki/Gascon_language" title="Gascon language">Gascon</a> was created.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Documentation on Bayonne for the period from the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a> are virtually nonexistent.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;Note 13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> with the exception of two Norman intrusions: one questionable in 844 and a second attested in 892.<sup id="cite_ref-p152_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p152-66">&#91;EG 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Labourd was created in 1023 Bayonne was the capital and the Viscount resided there.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;Note 14&#93;</a></sup> The history of Bayonne proper started in 1056 when Raymond II the Younger, Bishop of Bazas, had the mission to build the Church of Bayonne<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;Note 15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-p152_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p152-66">&#91;EG 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The construction was under the authority of Raymond III of Martres, <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Bayonne" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Bayonne">Bishop of Bayonne</a> from 1122 to 1125, combined with Viscount Bertrand for the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> cathedral, the rear of which can still be seen today, and the first wooden bridge across the Adour extending the Mayou bridge over the Nive, which inaugurated the heyday of Bayonne.<sup id="cite_ref-p152_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p152-66">&#91;EG 2&#93;</a></sup> From 1120 new districts were created under population pressure. The development of areas between the old Roman city of Grand Bayonne and the Nive also developed during this period, then between the Nive and the Adour at the place that became Petit Bayonne. A <a href="/wiki/Jacobin" title="Jacobin">Jacobin</a> Convent was located there in 1225 then that of the <a href="/wiki/Cordeliers" title="Cordeliers">Cordeliers</a> in 1247.<sup id="cite_ref-p152_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p152-66">&#91;EG 2&#93;</a></sup> Construction of and modifications to the defences of the city also developed to protect the new districts.<sup id="cite_ref-p9_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p9-69">&#91;PiH 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1130 the King of Aragon <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_the_Battler" title="Alfonso the Battler">Alfonso the Battler</a> besieged the city without success. Bayonne came under English rule when <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Aquitaine" title="Eleanor of Aquitaine">Eleanor of Aquitaine</a> married <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">Henry II of England</a> in 1152.<sup id="cite_ref-p6_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p6-70">&#91;PiH 3&#93;</a></sup> This alliance gave Bayonne many commercial privileges. The Bayonnaises became carriers of Bordeaux wines and other south-western products like resin, ham, and <a href="/wiki/Isatis_tinctoria" title="Isatis tinctoria">woad</a> to England.<sup id="cite_ref-p171_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p171-71">&#91;EG 3&#93;</a></sup> Bayonne was then an important military base. In 1177 King Richard separated the Viscounty of Labourd whose capital then became <a href="/wiki/Ustaritz" title="Ustaritz">Ustaritz</a>. Like many cities at the time, in 1215 Bayonne obtained the award of a municipal charter and was emancipated from feudal powers.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The official publication in 1273 of a <a href="/wiki/Coutume" title="Coutume">Coutume</a> unique to the city, remained in force for five centuries until the separation of Bayonne from Labourd.<sup id="cite_ref-p160_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p160-73">&#91;EG 4&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;Note 16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bayonnaise industry at that time was dominated by shipbuilding: wood (<a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chestnut" title="Chestnut">chestnut</a> from the Pyrenees, and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> from <a href="/wiki/Landes_forest" title="Landes forest">Landes</a>) being overabundant.<sup id="cite_ref-p162_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p162-75">&#91;EG 5&#93;</a></sup> There was also maritime activity in providing crews for <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a>, commercial marine or, and it was often so at a time when it was easy to turn any merchant ship into a warship, the English <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p163_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p163-76">&#91;EG 6&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;Note 17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance_and_modern_times">Renaissance and modern times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Renaissance and modern times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG/220px-Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG/330px-Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG/440px-Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_place_du_r%C3%A9duit_vue_de_la_citadelle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the ramparts overlooking the river.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Echauguette_(Bayonne).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Photographie d&#39;une \xc3\xa9chauguette de pierre blanche se d\xc3\xa9tachant au-dessus d&#39;un pont." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg/220px-Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg/330px-Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg/440px-Echauguette_%28Bayonne%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3312" data-file-height="4416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Echauguette_(Bayonne).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bartizan" title="Bartizan">Bartizan</a> on the Redoubt, restored in 2005.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_remparts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bayonne_remparts.jpg/220px-Bayonne_remparts.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bayonne_remparts.jpg/330px-Bayonne_remparts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Bayonne_remparts.jpg/440px-Bayonne_remparts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_remparts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ramparts of Bayonne.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Dunois" title="Jean de Dunois">Jean de Dunois</a> - a former companion at arms of <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" title="Joan of Arc">Joan of Arc</a>\xe2\x80\x94captured the city on 20 August 1451 and annexed it to the Crown "without making too many victims", but at the cost of a war indemnity of 40,000 gold <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cu" title="\xc3\x89cu">\xc3\x89cus</a> payable in a year,<sup id="cite_ref-p159_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p159-78">&#91;PH 3&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94thanks to the opportunism of the bishop who claimed to have seen "a large white cross surmounted by a crown which turns into a fleur-de-lis in the sky" to dissuade Bayonne from fighting against the royal troops.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;Note 18&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-p142_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p142-80">&#91;PH 4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The city continued to be fortified by the kings of France to protect it from danger from the Spanish border. In 1454 <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII</a> created a separate judicial district: the <i><a href="/wiki/Seneschal" title="Seneschal">Seneschal</a> of Lannes</i><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> a "single subdivision of <a href="/wiki/Guyenne" title="Guyenne">Guyenne</a> during the English period" which had jurisdiction over a wide area including Bayonne, <a href="/wiki/Dax,_Landes" title="Dax, Landes">Dax</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Sever" title="Saint-Sever">Saint-Sever</a> and which exercised civil justice, criminal jurisdiction within the competence of the district councilors. Over time, the "Seneschal of the Sword" which was at Dax lost any role other than protocol and Bayonne, along with Dax and Saint-Sever, became the de facto seat of a separate Seneschal under the authority of a "lieutenant-general of the Seneschal".<sup id="cite_ref-p160_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p160-82">&#91;PH 5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 1462 King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XI">Louis XI</a> authorized the holding of two annual fairs<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;Note 19&#93;</a></sup> by letters patent after signing the Treaty of Bayonne after which it was confirmed by the coutoumes of the inhabitants in July 1472 following the death of <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Valois,_Duke_de_Berry" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles de Valois, Duke de Berry">Charles de Valois, Duke de Berry</a>, the king\'s brother.<sup id="cite_ref-p164_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p164-84">&#91;PH 6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the time the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a> raged in the Iberian Peninsula Jews left Spain, and especially Portugal, then settled in Saint-Esprit. They brought with them <a href="/wiki/Chocolate" title="Chocolate">chocolate</a> and the recipe for its preparation.<sup id="cite_ref-p27_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p27-85">&#91;DN 2&#93;</a></sup> The golden age of the city ended in the 15th century with the loss of trade with England and the silting of the port of Bayonne created by the movement of the course of the Adour to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-p187_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p187-86">&#91;EG 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the beginning of the 16th century Labourd saw the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">plague</a>. Its path can be tracked by reading the <i>Registers</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In July 1515 the city of Bayonne was "prohibited to welcome people from plague-stricken places" and on 21 October, "we inhibit and prohibit all peasants and residents of this city [...] to go Parish Bidart [...] because of the contagion of the plague". On 11 April 1518 the plague raged in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Luz" title="Saint-Jean-de-Luz">Saint-Jean-de-Luz</a> and the city of Bayonne "inhibited and prohibited for all peasants and city inhabitants and other foreigners to maintain relationships at the location and Parish of Saint-Jean-de-Luz where people have died of the plague". On 11 November 1518 plague was present in Bayonne to the point that in 1519 the city council moved to the district of Brindos (Berindos at the time) in <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1523 Marshal <a href="/wiki/Odet_of_Foix,_Viscount_of_Lautrec" title="Odet of Foix, Viscount of Lautrec">Odet of Foix, Viscount of Lautrec</a> resisted the Spaniards under <a href="/wiki/Philibert_of_Chalon" title="Philibert of Chalon">Philibert of Chalon</a> in the service of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V_of_France" title="Charles V of France">Charles V</a> and lifted the siege of Bayonne.<sup id="cite_ref-p11_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p11-89">&#91;PiH 4&#93;</a></sup> It was at Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Vieux that the ransom demand for the release of Francis I, taken prisoner after his defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pavia" title="Battle of Pavia">Battle of Pavia</a>, was gathered.<sup id="cite_ref-p11_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p11-89">&#91;PiH 4&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;Note 20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The meeting in 1565 between <a href="/wiki/Catherine_de_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine de Medici">Catherine de Medici</a> and the envoy of <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a>: the Duke of Alba, is known as the <i>Interview of Bayonne</i>. At the time that <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> tore each other apart in parts of the kingdom of France, Bayonne seemed relatively untouched by these troubles.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> An iron fist from the city leaders did not appear to be unknown. In fact they never hesitated to use violence and criminal sanctions for keeping order in the name of the "public good".<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Two brothers, Saubat and Johannes Sorhaindo who were both lieutenants of the mayor of Bayonne in the second half of the 16th century, perfectly embody this period. They often wavered between Catholicism and Protestantism but always wanted to ensure the unity and prestige of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 16th century the king\'s engineers, under the direction of Louis de Foix, were dispatched to rearrange the course of the Adour by creating an estuary to maintain the river bed. The river discharged in the right place to the Ocean on 28 October 1578.}<sup id="cite_ref-p214_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p214-94">&#91;PH 7&#93;</a></sup> The port of Bayonne then attained a greater level of activity. Fishing for <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whale</a> ensured the wealth of fishermen and shipowners.\n</p><p>From 1611 to 1612 the college Principal of Bayonne was a man of 26 years old with a future: <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Jansen" title="Cornelius Jansen">Cornelius Jansen</a> known as <i>Jans\xc3\xa9nius</i>, the future <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Ypres" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Ypres">Bishop of Ypres</a>. Bayonne became the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Jansenism" title="Jansenism">Jansenism</a>, an austere science which strongly disrupted the monarchy of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the sporadic conflicts that troubled the French countryside from the mid 17th century, Bayonne peasants were short of powder and projectiles. They attached the long hunting knives in the barrels of their muskets and that way they fashioned makeshift spears later called <i><a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">bayonets</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In that same century, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9bastien_Le_Prestre_de_Vauban" title="S\xc3\xa9bastien Le Prestre de Vauban">Vauban</a> was charged by <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a> to fortify the city. He added a citadel built on a hill overlooking the district of <i>San Espirit Cap deou do Punt</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:662px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg/660px-Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg" width="660" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg/990px-Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg/1320px-Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10462" data-file-height="2380" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne-Le_r%C3%A9duit-20110309.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Redoubt, a system of fortifications destroyed at the beginning of the 20th century, seen from the Quaie de l\'Amiral-Lesseps.</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_Revolution_and_Empire">French Revolution and Empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: French Revolution and Empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Activity in Bayonne peaked in the 18th century. The Chamber of Commerce was founded in 1726.<sup id="cite_ref-p18_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p18-99">&#91;PiH 5&#93;</a></sup> Trade with <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a>, the cod fishery off the shores of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, and construction sites maintained a high level of activity in the port.<sup id="cite_ref-p511_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p511-100">&#91;PH 8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1792 the district of Saint-Esprit (that revolutionaries renamed <i>Port-de-la-Montagne</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> located on the right bank of the Adour, was separated from the city and renamed <i>Jean-Jacques Rousseau</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cassini_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cassini-102">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> It was reunited with Bayonne on 1 June 1857. For 65 years the autonomous commune was part of the department of <a href="/wiki/Landes_(department)" title="Landes (department)">Landes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p25_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p25-103">&#91;PiH 6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1808 at the Ch\xc3\xa2teau of Marracq the act of abdication of the Spanish king <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV</a> in favour of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> was signed under the "friendly pressure" of the Emperor. In the process the <a href="/wiki/Bayonne_Statute" title="Bayonne Statute">Bayonne Statute</a> was initialed as the first Spanish constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-p417_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p417-104">&#91;EG 8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in 1808 the French Empire imposed on the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw" title="Duchy of Warsaw">Duchy of Warsaw</a> the Convention of Bayonne to buy from France the debts owed to it by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MagocsiSedlar1974-49_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MagocsiSedlar1974-49-105">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The debt, amounting to more than 43 million <a href="/wiki/Franc" title="Franc">francs</a> in gold, was bought at a discounted rate of 21 million francs.<sup id="cite_ref-MagocsiSedlar1974-49_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MagocsiSedlar1974-49-105">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> However, although the duchy made its payments in installments to France over a four-year period, Prussia was unable to pay it (due to a very large indemnity it owed to France resulting from <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_Tilsit" title="Treaties of Tilsit">Treaties of Tilsit</a>), causing the Polish economy to suffer heavily.\n</p><p>Trade was the wealth of the city in the 18th century but suffered greatly in the 19th century, severely sanctioned by <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">conflict with Spain</a>, its historic trading partner in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-p24_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p24-106">&#91;PiH 7&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bayonne" title="Battle of Bayonne">Siege of Bayonne</a> marked the end of the period with the surrender of the Napoleonic troops of Marshal <a href="/wiki/Jean-de-Dieu_Soult" title="Jean-de-Dieu Soult">Jean-de-Dieu Soult</a> who were defeated by the coalition led by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Wellington</a> on 5 May 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-p418_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p418-107">&#91;EG 9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_period">Contemporary period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Contemporary period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg/330px-CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg" width="330" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg/495px-CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg/660px-CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1648" data-file-height="1064" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CAP_39_-_BAYONNE_-_La_Gare.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The second <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Bayonne" title="Gare de Bayonne">Gare de Bayonne</a>, photographed here in the 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;Note 21&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1854 the railway arrived from Paris bringing many tourists eager to enjoy the beaches of <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>. Bayonne turned instead to the <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a> industry with the forges of the Adour.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;Note 22&#93;</a></sup> The Port took on an industrial look but its slow decline seemed inexorable in the 19th century. The discovery of the Lacq gas field restored a certain dynamism.\n</p><p>The Treaty of Bayonne was concluded on 2 December 1856. It overcame the disputes in fixing the Franco-Spanish border in the area extending from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Bidassoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Bidassoa">Bidassoa</a> to the border between <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a>.\n</p><p>The city built three light railway lines to connect to Biarritz at the beginning of the 20th century. The most direct line, that of the <i>Tramway Bayonne-Lyc\xc3\xa9e\xe2\x80\x93Biarritz</i> was operated from 1888 to 1948. In addition a line further north served Anglet, operated by the <i>Chemin de fer Bayonne-Anglet-Biarritz</i> company from 1877 to 1953. Finally a line following the Adour to its mouth and to the Atlantic Ocean by the bar in Anglet, was operated by <i>VFDM r\xc3\xa9seau basque</i> from 1919 to 1948.\n</p><p>On the morning of 23 December 1933, sub-prefect Anthelme received Gustave Tissier, the director of the <i>Cr\xc3\xa9dit Municipal de Bayonne</i>. He responded well, with some astonishment, to his persistent interview. It did not surprise him to see the man unpacking what became the scam of the century.\n</p><p>"Tissier, director of the <i>Cr\xc3\xa9dit Municipal</i>, was arrested and imprisoned under suspicion of forgery and misappropriation of public funds. He had issued thousands of false bonds in the name of <i>Cr\xc3\xa9dit Municipal</i> [...]"<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;Note 23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>This was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Stavisky_Affair" title="Stavisky Affair">Stavisky Affair</a> which, together with other scandals and political crises, led to the Paris riots of 6 February 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_World_Wars">The World Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The World Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 249th Infantry Regiment, created from the 49th Infantry Regiment, was engaged in operations in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, including action at <a href="/wiki/Chemin_des_Dames" title="Chemin des Dames">Chemin des Dames</a>, especially on the plateau of <a href="/wiki/Craonne" title="Craonne">Craonne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-p54_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p54-113">&#91;FL 3&#93;</a></sup> 700 Bayonnaises perished in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-p54_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p54-113">&#91;FL 3&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;Note 24&#93;</a></sup> A centre for engagement of foreign volunteers was established in August 1914 in Bayonne. Many nationalities were represented, particularly the Spanish, the Portuguese, the Czechs,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;Note 25&#93;</a></sup> and the Poles<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;Note 26&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-p55_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p55-117">&#91;FL 4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> Bayonne was occupied by the <a href="/wiki/3rd_SS_Panzer_Division_Totenkopf" title="3rd SS Panzer Division Totenkopf">3rd SS Panzer Division Totenkopf</a> from 27 June 1940 to 23 August 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-p30_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-p30-118">&#91;PiH 8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 April 1942 the Allies made a landing attempt in Bayonne but after a barge penetrated the Adour with great difficulty, the operation was canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 August 1944, after blowing up twenty ships in port,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> German troops withdrew. On the 22nd a final convoy of five vehicles passed through the city. It transported Gestapo Customs agents and some elements of the <i>Feldgendarmerie</i>. One or more Germans opened fire with machine guns killing three people.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;Note 27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> On the 23rd there was an informal and immediate installation of a "special municipal delegation" by the young deputy prefect Guy Lamassoure representing the <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Government_of_the_French_Republic" title="Provisional Government of the French Republic">Provisional Government of the French Republic</a> which had been established in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> since 27 June.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Heraldry">Heraldry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Heraldry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;padding:5px 8px;width:120px;"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Blason_Bayonne.svg" class="image" title="Arms of Bayonne"><img alt="Arms of Bayonne" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blason_Bayonne.svg/120px-Blason_Bayonne.svg.png" width="120" height="132" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blason_Bayonne.svg/180px-Blason_Bayonne.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Blason_Bayonne.svg/240px-Blason_Bayonne.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="660" /></a></div></div>\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top;"><a href="/wiki/Paul_Raymond_(archivist)" title="Paul Raymond (archivist)">Paul Raymond</a> noted in 1863 that the arms of the city were blazoned:\n<p><i>Azure, a tower embattled and ramparted of Argent, wavy proper in base, cantoned to dexter with a letter N crowned of Or, between two pines Vert each fructed of seven Or and set with fruit pal, debruised by two lions langued confronting.<sup id="cite_ref-Raymond_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raymond-42">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></i>\n</p><p><b>The current arms are Blazoned:</b><br /><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;Note 28&#93;</a></sup> \n<i>Gules, a tower turreted of Or, masooned, windowed, and porte of Sable on a sea wavy of Azure, Or and Sable in base and surmounted by a fleur-de-lis of Or, between two oaks proper fructed seven of Or debruised by two lions langued confronting of Or; the arms stamped with a county crown.</i>\n</p><p><br />\n</p><p><br />\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Policy_and_Administration">Policy and Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Policy and Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="List_of_mayors_under_the_Ancien_R.C3.A9gime"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_mayors_under_the_Ancien_R\xc3\xa9gime">List of mayors under the Ancien R\xc3\xa9gime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: List of mayors under the Ancien R\xc3\xa9gime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Gramont" title="Duke of Gramont">Gramont family</a> provided captains and governors in Bayonne from 1472 to 1789 as well as mayors, a post which became hereditary from 28 January 1590 by concession of <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV</a> to Antoine II of Gramont. From the 15th century they resided in the Ch\xc3\xa2teau Neuf then in the Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Vieux from the end of the 16th century:<sup id="cite_ref-Bayonne_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayonne-124">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;Note 29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Roger de Gramont</b>, (1444\xe2\x80\x931519), Lord of Gramont, Baron of Haux, Seneschal of Guyenne, hereditary mayor of Bayonne. He was an advisor and chamberlain of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XI">Louis XI</a> in 1472 and then <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">Charles VIII</a> in 1483. He was Ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XII">Louis XII</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> in 1502. He became governor of Bayonne and its castles on 26 February 1487. He died of the plague in 1519.<sup id="cite_ref-Bayonne_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayonne-124">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Jean II de Gramont</b>, Lord of Gramont, mayor and captain of Bayonne from 18 March 1523. On 15 September 1523, as a lieutenant in the company of <a href="/wiki/Odet_of_Foix,_Viscount_of_Lautrec" title="Odet of Foix, Viscount of Lautrec">Marshal Lautrec</a>, he rescued Bayonne from the siege by the forces of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a> under the command of the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Orange" title="Prince of Orange">Prince of Orange</a>. He died during the wars in Italy;<sup id="cite_ref-Bayonne_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayonne-124">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Antoine I of Gramont</b>, born in 1526, he was appointed at the age of nine years (1535) as mayor and captain of Bayonne. In 1571 he charged Louis de Foix with the changes to the mouth of the Adour along the fortifications of the city;</li>\n<li><b>Antoine II de Gramont</b> (1572\xe2\x80\x931644), Count of Gramont, Guiche and Toulonjon, Viscount then Count of Louvigny, ruler of Bidache, Viscount of Aster, lord then baron of Lescun. He was a <i>Duke de Brevet</i> in 1643, but unverified by Parliament. On 28 January 1590 <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV</a> granted him and his descendants the perpetual office of Mayor of Bayonne. He then became the Viceroy of Navarre. In 1595, Antoine II de Gramont charged Jean Errard (1599) then Louis de Millet (1612) to strengthen the defenses of the city;</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Antoine_III_de_Gramont" title="Antoine III de Gramont">Antoine III of Gramont-Touloujon</a></b> (1604\xe2\x80\x931678), Count and then, in 1648, Duke of Gramont, Prince of Bidache, Count of Guiche, Toulonjon, and Louvigny, Viscount of Astern, Baron of Andouins and Hagetmau, and lord of Lesparre, peer of France in 1648, <a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshal of France">Marshal of France</a> in 1641. As Ambassador of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, in 1660 he sought the hand of the <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Spain" title="Maria Theresa of Spain">Infanta Maria Theresa</a>. The king gave him power of attorney to represent him in the marriage which was celebrated in Madrid. It was he who welcomed Louis XIV, <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Austria" title="Anne of Austria">Anne of Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Mazarin" title="Cardinal Mazarin">Mazarin</a>, and the rest of the Court to Bayonne. He died on 12 July 1678 at the Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Vieux;<sup id="cite_ref-Bayonne_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayonne-124">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Antoine_Charles_IV_de_Gramont" title="Antoine Charles IV de Gramont">Antoine Charles IV of Gramont</a></b> (1641\xe2\x80\x931720), Duke of Gramont, Prince of Bidache, Count of Guiche and Louvigny, Viscount of Aster, Baron of Andouins and Hagetmau, Lord of Lesparre, peer of France, Viceroy of Navarre. In 1689, he continued the fortification works undertaken by <a href="/wiki/Vauban" class="mw-redirect" title="Vauban">Vauban</a> in Bayonne, where he remained from 1706 to 1712. He supported <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_France" title="Philip V of France">Philip V</a> during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, using Bayonne to supply his troops, weapons, reinforcements and subsidies. In retaliation, the opponents of Philip V organized two attacks in 1707: one at Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Vieux leaving Antoine IV unharmed.<sup id="cite_ref-Bayonne_124-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bayonne-124">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_times">Modern times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Modern times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>List of Successive <a href="/wiki/Mayor_(France)" title="Mayor (France)">Mayors</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;"><div Basterreche\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1833</td>\n<td>1848</td>\n<td>Fran\xc3\xa7ois Balasque\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1848</td>\n<td>1849</td>\n<td>Eug\xc3\xa8ne Boutouey\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1849</td>\n<td>1850</td>\n<td>Joachim Alexandre Dubrocq\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1852</td>\n<td>1869</td>\n<td>Jules 2008\xe2\x80\x932014\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2014</td>\n<td>2020</td>\n<td>Jean Ren\xc3\xa9 Etchegaray</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Union_of_Democrats_and_Independents" title="Union of Democrats and Independents">UDI</a></td>\n<td>President of the Adour-Basque Coast agglomeration\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>(Not all data is known)\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cantons_of_Bayonne">Cantons of Bayonne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cantons of Bayonne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As per the Decree of 22 December 1789 Bayonne was part of two cantons: Bayonne-North-east, which includes part of Bayonne commune plus <a href="/wiki/Boucau" title="Boucau">Boucau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pierre-d%27Irube" title="Saint-Pierre-d&#39;Irube">Saint-Pierre-d\'Irube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lahonce" title="Lahonce">Lahonce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mouguerre" title="Mouguerre">Mouguerre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urcuit" title="Urcuit">Urcuit</a>; and Bayonne Northwest which consisted of the rest of Bayonne commune plus <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcangues" title="Arcangues">Arcangues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bassussarry" title="Bassussarry">Bassussarry</a>.\n</p><p>In a first revision of cantons in 1973 three cantons were created from the same total; geographic area: Bayonne North, Bayonne East, and Bayonne West. A further reconfiguration in 1982 focused primarily on Bayonne and, apart from Bayonne North Canton, which also includes Boucau, the cantons of Bayonne East and Bayonne West did not change.\n</p><p>Starting from the <a href="/wiki/French_departmental_elections,_2015" title="French departmental elections, 2015">French departmental elections, 2015</a> which took place on 22 and 29 March, a new division took effect following the decree of 25 February 2014<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Once again three cantons centred on Bayonne are defined: <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Bayonne-1" title="Canton of Bayonne-1">Bayonne-1</a>\xe2\x80\x94with part of Anglet; <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Bayonne-2" title="Canton of Bayonne-2">Bayonne-2</a>\xe2\x80\x94which includes Boucau; and <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Bayonne-3" title="Canton of Bayonne-3">Bayonne-3</a> now define the cantonal territorial division of the area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_and_administrative_proceedings">Judicial and administrative proceedings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Judicial and administrative proceedings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne is the seat of many courts for the region. It falls under the jurisdiction of the <i><a href="/wiki/Tribunal_d%27instance" title="Tribunal d&#39;instance">Tribunal d\'instance</a></i> (District court) of Bayonne, the <i>Tribunal de grande instance</i> (High Court) of Bayonne, the <i>Cour d\'appel</i> (<a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_(France)" title="Court of Appeal (France)">Court of Appeal</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Pau,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Pau, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Pau</a>, the <i>Tribunal pour enfants</i> (<a href="/wiki/Juvenile_court" title="Juvenile court">Juvenile court</a>) of Bayonne, the <i><a href="/wiki/Conseil_de_prud%27hommes" class="mw-redirect" title="Conseil de prud&#39;hommes">Conseil de prud\'hommes</a></i> (Labour Court) of Bayonne, the <i><a href="/wiki/Tribunal_de_commerce" title="Tribunal de commerce">Tribunal de commerce</a></i> (Commercial Court) of Bayonne, the <i>Tribunal administratif</i> (Administrative tribunal) of <a href="/wiki/Pau,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Pau, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Pau</a>, and the <i>Cour administrative d\'appel</i> (Administrative Court of Appeal) of <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The commune has a <a href="/wiki/Police_station" title="Police station">police station</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Departmental_Gendarmerie" title="Departmental Gendarmerie">Departmental Gendarmerie</a>, an Autonomous Territorial Brigade of the district gendarmerie, squadron 24/2 of <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Gendarmerie" title="Mobile Gendarmerie">Mobile Gendarmerie</a> and a Tax collection office.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intercommunality">Intercommunality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Intercommunality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The commune is part of twelve inter-communal structures of which eleven are based in the commune:<sup id="cite_ref-Interco_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interco-129">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>the C\xc3\xb4te basque-Adour Agglomeration;</li>\n<li>the transport association of C\xc3\xb4te basque-Adour Agglomeration (STACBA);</li>\n<li>the intercommunal association for the management of the Txakurrak centre;</li>\n<li>the intercommunal association for the support of Basque culture;</li>\n<li>the Bil Ta Garbi joint association;</li>\n<li>the joint association for maritime Nive;</li>\n<li>the joint association for the Basque Museum and the History of Bayonne;</li>\n<li>the joint association for the development and monitoring of SCOT in the agglomeration of Bayonne and south Landes;</li>\n<li>the Kosta Garbia joint association;</li>\n<li>the joint association for the development of the European freight centre of Bayonne-Mouguerre-Lahonce;</li>\n<li>the joint association for operating the regional Maurice Ravel Conservatory.</li>\n<li>the Energy association of Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques;</li></ul>\n<p>The city of Bayonne is part of the <i>Agglomeration C\xc3\xb4te Basque-Adour</i> which also includes Anglet, Biarritz, Bidart and Boucau. The statutory powers of the structure extend to economic development\xe2\x80\x94including higher education and research\xe2\x80\x94housing and urban planning, public transport\xe2\x80\x94through Transdev\xe2\x80\x94alternative and the collection and recovery waste collection and management of rain and coastal waters, the sustainable development, interregional cooperation and finally 106.\n</p><p>In addition Bayonne is part of the Basque Bayonne-San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n Eurocity which is a <a href="/wiki/European_economic_interest_grouping" title="European economic interest grouping">European economic interest grouping</a> (EEIG) established in 1993 based in <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n">San Sebasti\xc3\xa1n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurocit\xc3\xa9_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurocit\xc3\xa9-130">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_\xe2\x80\x93_Sister_cities">Twin towns towns \xe2\x80\x93 Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2012 the commune had 45,855 inhabitants. The evolution of the number of inhabitants is known from the population censuses conducted in the commune since 1793. From the 21st century, a census of communes with fewer than 10,000 inhabitants is held every five years, unlike larger communes that have a sample survey every year.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;Note 30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<center><b>Population change</b> <small><a tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:477px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Population_-_Municipality_code_64102.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Population_-_Municipality_code_64102.svg/475px-Population_-_Municipality_code_64102.svg.png" width="475" height="355" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="475" data-file-height="355" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><b>Population of Bayonne</b></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne commune is attached to the Academy of Bordeaux. It has an information and guidance center (CIO).<sup id="cite_ref-Education_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Education-134">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 December 2015 Bayonne had 10 kindergartens, 22 elementary or primary schools (12 public and 10 private primary schools including two ikastolas). 2 public colleges (Albert Camus and Marracq colleges), 5 private colleges (La Salle Saint-Bernard, Saint Joseph, Saint-Amand, Notre-Dame and Largent\xc3\xa9) which meet the criteria of the first cycle of second degree studies. For the second cycle Bayonne has 3 public high schools (Ren\xc3\xa9-Cassin school (general education), the Louis de Foix school (general, technological and vocational education), and the Paul Bert vocational school), 4 private high schools (Saint-Louis Villa Pia (general education), Largent\xc3\xa9, Bernat Etxepare (general and technological), and Le Guichot vocational school).\n</p><p>There are also the Maurice Ravel Conservatory of Music, Dance, and Dramatic Art and the art school of the urban community of Bayonne-Anglet-Biarritz.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_festivities_and_events">Cultural festivities and events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cultural festivities and events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg/330px-Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Roi_L%C3%A9on.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>F\xc3\xaates de Bayonne 2004, King L\xc3\xa9on.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArenesBayonnes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/ArenesBayonnes.jpg/220px-ArenesBayonnes.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/ArenesBayonnes.jpg/330px-ArenesBayonnes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/ArenesBayonnes.jpg/440px-ArenesBayonnes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4655" data-file-height="2505" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArenesBayonnes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bayonne Bullfighting ring</div></div></div>\n<p>For 550 years every holy Thursday, Friday and Saturday the <i>Foire au Jambon</i> (Ham festival) is held to mark the beginning of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;Note 31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An annual summer festival has been held in the commune since 1932 for five days<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;Note 32&#93;</a></sup> organized around parades, bulls races, <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a>, and music in the Basque and Gascon tradition. These festivals have become the most important festive events in France in terms of attendance.\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/F%C3%AAtes_de_Bayonne" title="F\xc3\xaates de Bayonne">F\xc3\xaates de Bayonne</a></div>\n<p>Bayonne has the oldest French bullfighting tradition. A bylaw regulating the <i>encierro</i> is dated 1283: cows, oxen and bulls are released each year in the streets of Petit Bayonne during the summer festivals. The current arena, opened in 1893, is the largest in South-west France with more than 10,000 seats. A dozen bullfights are held each year, attracting the biggest names in bullfighting. Throughout summer several <i>novilladas</i> also take place. The city is a member of the <i>Union of French bullfighting cities</i>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne is the focus of much of the hospital services for the agglomeration of Bayonne and the southern Landes. In this area all inhabitants are less than 35&#160;km from a hospital offering medical, obstetrical, surgical, or psychiatric care. The hospitals for all the Basque Coast are mainly established in Bayonne (the main site of Saint-L\xc3\xa9on and Cam-de-Prats) and also in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Luz" title="Saint-Jean-de-Luz">Saint-Jean-de-Luz</a> which has several clinics.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_and_sports_facilities">Sports and sports facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports and sports facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg/330px-Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Aviron_Bayonnais.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bayonne Rowing Boat shed</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><b>Rowing</b>, a popular sport for a long time on the Nive and the Adour near Bayonne. There are two clubs: the Nautical Society of Bayonne (SNB) (established in 1875) and <i>Aviron Bayonnais</i>\xe2\x80\x94established in 1904 by former members of the SNB and which later became a sports club.</li>\n<li><b>Basketball</b>. <i>Denek Bat Bayonne Urcuit</i> is a basketball club with a male section competing in NM1 (3rd national level of the French league). The club is based in the city of <a href="/wiki/Urcuit" title="Urcuit">Urcuit</a> but plays in the Lauga Sports Palace in Bayonne.</li>\n<li><b>Football</b>. <a href="/wiki/Aviron_Bayonnais_FC" title="Aviron Bayonnais FC">Aviron Bayonnais FC</a> play their home games at Didier Deschamps Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Championnat_National_3" title="Championnat National 3">Championnat National 3</a> (the 5th French division) since the 2013\xe2\x80\x932014 season after a year in CFA and three consecutive years in the <a href="/wiki/Championnat_National" title="Championnat National">Championnat National</a>. <a href="/wiki/Didier_Deschamps" title="Didier Deschamps">Didier Deschamps</a> started his career at Aviron Bayonnais FC. The stadium, formerly called the <i>Grand Basque</i>, is now named after him. There are also three other football clubs in Bayonne: the <i>Crusaders of Saint Andrew</i> playing in the higher regional division, the <i>Portuguese stars of Bayonne</i> (first district division), and the Bayonne association on the right bank of the river (3rd district division).</li>\n<li><b>Omnisports</b>. Aviron Bayonnais, created in 1904, includes many sports sections and a large number of members.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;Note 33&#93;</a></sup> The pro rugby and football club are the most famous sections of the club. The <i>Bayonne Olympic Club</i>, created in 1972, is located in the district of Hauts de Sainte-Croix. The club offers a wide range of sports including <a href="/wiki/Pelote" class="mw-redirect" title="Pelote">pelote</a>, gymnastics, combat sports, and a <a href="/wiki/Pool_(cue_sports)" title="Pool (cue sports)">pool</a> section. The club had nearly 400 members in 2007.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Basque_Pelota" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Pelota">Basque Pelota</a></b> Bayonne is an important place for Basque pelota. The <i>French Federation of Basque Pelota</i> is headquartered at <i>Trinquet moderne</i> near the Bullring.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Many titles were won by pelota players from the city. The World Championships took place in Bayonne in 1978 in association with Biarritz.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Rugby</b> appeared in Basque Country at the end of the 19th century with the arrival in 1897 at Bayonne High School of a 20 year old person from Landes who converts his comrades to football-rugby which he had discovered in Bordeaux.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Practicing in the fields near the Spanish Gate, they communicated their enthusiasm to other colleges in Bayonne and Biarritz leading to the creation of the Biarritz Sporting Club and Biarritz Stadium which merged in 1913 to become <a href="/wiki/Biarritz_Olympique" title="Biarritz Olympique">Biarritz Olympique</a>. Bayonne has two rugby clubs: The Bayonne Athletic Association (ASB) plays in <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_3" title="F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9rale 3">F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9rale 3</a> while the Aviron Bayonnais rugby pro in the 2014\xe2\x80\x932015 season played in <a href="/wiki/Top_14" title="Top 14">Top 14</a>, where they have played without interruption since the 2004\xe2\x80\x932005 season. Aviron Bayonnais has won three league titles in France (1913, 1934 and 1943). It was the first club from a small town to become champion of France. Its stadium is the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Jean_Dauger" title="Stade Jean Dauger">Stade Jean Dauger</a>. There is also a women\'s team in the ASB, playing in the National Division 1B. This team won the 2014 Armelle Auclair challenge.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worship">Worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Catholic_worship">Catholic worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Catholic worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Bayonne is in the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Bayonne" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Bayonne">Diocese of Bayonne</a>, Lescar and Oloron, with a <a href="/wiki/Suffragan_bishop" title="Suffragan bishop">Suffragan bishop</a> since 2002 under the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Bordeaux" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Bordeaux">Archdiocese of Bordeaux</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Monseigneur <a href="/wiki/Marc_Aillet" title="Marc Aillet">Marc Aillet</a> has been the bishop of this diocese since 15 October 2008. The diocese is located in Bayonne in the Place Monseigneur-Vansteenberghe.\n</p><p>Besides <a href="/wiki/Bayonne_Cathedral" title="Bayonne Cathedral">Bayonne Cathedral</a> in Grand Bayonne, Bayonne has Saint-Esprit, Saint Andrew (Rue des Lisses), Ar\xc3\xa8nes (Avenue of the Czech Legion), Saint-\xc3\x89tienne, and Saint-Amand (Avenue Marechal Soult) churches.\n</p><p>The <i>Carmel of Bayonne</i>, located in the Marracq district, has had a community of <a href="/wiki/Carmelite" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmelite">Carmelite</a> nuns since 1858.\n</p><p>The <i>Way of Baztan</i> (also <i>ruta del Baztan</i> or <i>camino Baztan\xc3\xa9s</i>) is a way on the pilgrimage of <a href="/wiki/Camino_de_Santiago" title="Camino de Santiago">Camino de Santiago</a> which crosses the Pyrenees further west by the lowest pass (by the <i>Col de Belate</i>, 847&#160;m). It is the ancient road used by pilgrims descending to Bayonne then either along the coast on the <i>Way of Soulac</i> or because they landed there from England, for example, to join the <a href="/wiki/French_Way" title="French Way">French Way</a> as soon as possible in <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>. The <i>Way of Bayonne</i> joins the French Way further downstream at <a href="/wiki/Burgos" title="Burgos">Burgos</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Jewish_worship">Jewish worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Jewish worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogue</a> was built in 1837 in the Saint-Esprit district north of the town.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The Jewish community of Bayonne is old\xe2\x80\x94it consists of different groups of fugitives from Navarre and Portugal who established at SAint-Esprit-l\xc3\xa8s-Bayonne after the expulsion of Jews from Spain in 1492 and Portugal in 1496. In 1846 the <a href="/wiki/Central_Consistory" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Consistory">Central Consistory</a> moved to Saint-Esprit which was integrated with Bayonne in 1857.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_worship">Muslim worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Muslim worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The mosque is located in Rue Joseph-Latxague. It is the seat of the cultural association of Muslims in the Basque Coast.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestant_worship">Protestant worship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Protestant worship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Protestant church is located at the corner of Rue Albert-I st and Rue du Temple<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> A gospel church is located in the Saint-Esprit districtit where there is also a church belonging to the <a href="/wiki/Gypsy" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsy">Gypsy</a> Evangelical Church of the Protestant Federation of France.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Poissonnerie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rue Poissonnerie, a shopping street in Grand-Bayonne.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Biarritz_Jambon_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Biarritz_Jambon_%281%29.jpg/150px-Biarritz_Jambon_%281%29.jpg" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" ham</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:188px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Piment_4_det.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Piment_4_det.gif" width="186" height="195" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="186" data-file-height="195" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Piment_4_det.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dark Chocolate with <a href="/wiki/Espelette_pepper" title="Espelette pepper">Espelette pepper</a>.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_income_tax">Population and income tax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Population and income tax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2011, the median household income tax was \xe2\x82\xac22,605, placing Bayonne 28,406th place among the 31,886 communes with more than 49 households in metropolitan France.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011 47.8% of households were not taxable.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;Insee 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jobs">Jobs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Jobs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2011 the population aged from 15 to 64 years was 29,007 persons of which 70.8% were employable, 60.3% in employment and 10.5% unemployed.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;Insee 2&#93;</a></sup> While there were 30,012 jobs in the employment area, against 29,220 in 2006, and the number of employed workers residing in the employment area was 17,667, the indicator of job concentration is 169.9% which means that the employment area offers nearly two jobs to for every available worker.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;Insee 3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Businesses_and_shops">Businesses and shops</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Businesses and shops">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne is the economic capital of the agglomeration of Bayonne and southern Landes. The table below details the number of companies located in Bayonne according to their industry:<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;Insee 4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable centre" style="text-align:center;">\n<caption>Structure of the Economy in Bayonne as at 1 January 2013.\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col" style="background: #DDFFDD;
