color:black;">Public Administration, education, health, social services\n</th>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">1,227\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">20.6\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">920\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">171\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">47\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">50\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFFFFF; color:black;">39\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="8" style="text-align:center;font-size:90%;">Scope: All activities.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The following comments apply to the two previous tables:<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;Note 34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>the bulk of economic activity is provided by companies in the tertiary sector;</li>\n<li>Agriculture is almost non-existent Note 54;<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;Note 35&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>less than 5% of the activity is from the industrial sector which remains focused on establishments of less than 50 employees, as also are construction-related activities;</li>\n<li>public administration, education, health and social services are activities of over 20% of establishments, confirming the importance of Bayonne as an administrative centre.</li></ul>\n<p>In 2013 549 new establishments were created in Bayonne including 406 <a href="/wiki/Sole_proprietorship" title="Sole proprietorship">Sole proprietorships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;Insee 6&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;Insee 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Workshops_and_Industry">Workshops and Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Workshops and Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Bayonne has few such industries, as indicated in the previous tables. There is <i>Plastitube</i> specializing in plastic packaging (190 employees).<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Izarra_(liqueur)" title="Izarra (liqueur)">Izarra</a> liqueur company set up a distillery in 1912 at Quai Amiral-Bergeret and has long symbolized the economic wealth of Bayonne. Industrial activities are concentrated in the neighbouring communes of <a href="/wiki/Boucau" title="Boucau">Boucau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tarnos" title="Tarnos">Tarnos</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turbomeca" class="mw-redirect" title="Turbomeca">Turbomeca</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mouguerre" title="Mouguerre">Mouguerre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anglet" title="Anglet">Anglet</a>.\n</p><p>Bayonne is known for its fine chocolates, produced in the town for 500 years, and Bayonne ham, a cured ham seasoned with peppers from nearby <a href="/wiki/Espelette" title="Espelette">Espelette</a>. <a href="/wiki/Izarra_(liqueur)" title="Izarra (liqueur)">Izarra</a>, the liqueur made in bright green or yellow colours, is distilled locally. It is said by some that Bayonne is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Mayonnaise" title="Mayonnaise">mayonnaise</a>, supposedly a corruption of <i>Bayonnaise</i>, the French adjective describing the city\'s people and produce. Now bayonnaise can refer to a particular mayonnaise flavoured with the Espelette chillis.\n</p><p>Bayonne is now the centre of certain craft industries that were once widespread, including the manufacture of <i><a href="/wiki/Makila" title="Makila">makilas</a></i>, traditional Basque walking-sticks. The Fabrique Alza just outside the city is known for its <i>palas</i>, bats used in <i><a href="/wiki/Basque_pelota" title="Basque pelota">pelota</a></i>, the traditional Basque sport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_activities">Service activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Service activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The active tertiary sector includes some large retail chains such as those detailed by geographer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Brunet" title="Roger Brunet">Roger Brunet</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> BUT (240 staff), <a href="/wiki/Carrefour" title="Carrefour">Carrefour</a> (150 staff), <a href="/wiki/E.Leclerc" title="E.Leclerc">E.Leclerc</a> (150 staff), <a href="/wiki/Leroy_Merlin" title="Leroy Merlin">Leroy Merlin</a> (130 staff), and <a href="/wiki/Galeries_Lafayette" title="Galeries Lafayette">Galeries Lafayette</a> (120 employees). Banks, cleaning companies (Onet, 170 employees), and security (<a href="/wiki/Brink%27s" title="Brink&#39;s">Brink\'s</a>, 100 employees) are also major employers in the commune, as is urban transport which employs nearly 200 staff. Five health clinics, providing a total of more than 500 beds, each employ 120 to 170 staff.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_port_of_Bayonne">The port of Bayonne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: The port of Bayonne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg/220px-BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg/330px-BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg/440px-BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4540" data-file-height="2554" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBC-Magellan_%C3%A0_Bayonne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cargo ship <i>BBC-Magellan</i> in the port of Bayonne in 2014.</div></div></div>\n<p>The port of Bayonne is located at the mouth of the Adour, downstream of the city. It also occupies part of communes of Anglet and Boucau in <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees-Atlantiques" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyrenees-Atlantiques">Pyrenees-Atlantiques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarnos" title="Tarnos">Tarnos</a> in <a href="/wiki/Landes_(department)" title="Landes (department)">Landes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> It benefits greatly from the natural gas field of Lacq to which it is connected by pipeline. This is the 9th largest French port for trade with an annual traffic of about 4.2 million tonnes of which 2.8 is export. It is also the largest French port for export of <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> It is the property of the Aquitaine region who manage and control the site.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Metallurgical products movement are more than one million tons per year and maize exports to Spain vary between 800,000 and 1 million tons. The port also receives refined oil products from the <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">Total</a> oil refinery at <a href="/wiki/Donges" title="Donges">Donges</a> (800,000 tons per year). Fertilizers are a traffic of 500,000 tons per year and <a href="/wiki/Sulphur" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulphur">sulphur</a> from Lacq, albeit in sharp decline, is 400,000 tons.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The port also receives <a href="/wiki/Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> vehicles from Spain and Portugal and wood both tropical and from Landes.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunet_138-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunet-138">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_services">Tourism services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Tourism services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Due to its proximity to the ocean and the foothills of the Pyrenees as well as its historic heritage, Bayonne has developed important activities related to tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;Insee 8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 December 2012 there were 15 hotels in the city offering more than 800 rooms to visitors, but there were no camp sites.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;Insee 9&#93;</a></sup> The tourist infrastructure in the surrounding urban area of Bayonne complements the local supply with around 5800 rooms spread over nearly 200 hotels and 86 campsites offering over 14,000 beds.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sights">Sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_castle,_Bayonne,_Pyrenees,_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg/220px-Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg/330px-Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg/440px-Old_castle%2C_Bayonne%2C_Pyrenees%2C_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3472" data-file-height="2608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_castle,_Bayonne,_Pyrenees,_France-LCCN2001698608.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Ch\xc3\xa2teau Vieux</div></div></div>\n<p>The Nive divides Bayonne into Grand Bayonne and Petit Bayonne with five bridges between the two, both quarters still being backed by <a href="/wiki/Vauban" class="mw-redirect" title="Vauban">Vauban</a>\'s walls. The houses lining the Nive are examples of Basque architecture, with half-timbering and shutters in the national colours of red and green. The much wider Adour is to the north. The Pont Saint-Esprit connects Petit Bayonne with the Quartier Saint-Esprit across the <a href="/wiki/Adour" title="Adour">Adour</a>, where the massive Citadelle and the railway station are located. Grand Bayonne is the commercial and civic hub, with small pedestrianised streets packed with shops, plus the cathedral and <a href="/wiki/City_and_town_halls" class="mw-redirect" title="City and town halls">H\xc3\xb4tel de Ville</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bayonne_Cathedral" title="Bayonne Cathedral">Cath\xc3\xa9drale Sainte-Marie</a> is an imposing, elegant <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> building, rising over the houses, glimpsed along the narrow streets. It was constructed in the 12th and 13th centuries. The south tower was completed in the 16th century but the cathedral was only completed in the 19th century with the north tower. The cathedral is noted for its charming <a href="/wiki/Cloister" title="Cloister">cloisters</a>. There are other details and sculptures of note, although much was destroyed in the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">Revolution</a>.\n</p><p>Nearby is the Ch\xc3\xa2teau Vieux, some of which dates back to the 12th century, where the governors of the city were based, including the English <a href="/wiki/Edward,_the_Black_Prince" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward, the Black Prince">Black Prince</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BayonneCatedral.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BayonneCatedral.JPG/220px-BayonneCatedral.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BayonneCatedral.JPG/330px-BayonneCatedral.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/BayonneCatedral.JPG/440px-BayonneCatedral.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BayonneCatedral.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sainte-Marie Cathedral</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mus\xc3\xa9e Basque is the finest ethnographic museum of the entire Basque Country. It opened in 1922 but has been closed for a decade recently for refurbishment. It now has special exhibitions on Basque agriculture, seafaring and <i><a href="/wiki/Basque_pelota" title="Basque pelota">pelota</a></i>, handicrafts and Basque history and way of life.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Bonnat" title="Mus\xc3\xa9e Bonnat">Mus\xc3\xa9e Bonnat</a> began with a large collection bequeathed by the local-born painter <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Bonnat" title="L\xc3\xa9on Bonnat">L\xc3\xa9on Bonnat</a>. The museum is one of the best galleries in south west France and has paintings by <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Degas" title="Edgar Degas">Edgar Degas</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">Sandro Botticelli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Goya" title="Francisco Goya">Francisco Goya</a>, among others.\n</p><p>At the back of Petit Bayonne is the Ch\xc3\xa2teau Neuf, among the ramparts. Now an exhibition space, it was started by the newly arrived French in 1460 to control the city. The walls nearby have been opened to visitors. They are important for plant life now and Bayonne\'s <a href="/wiki/Jardin_botanique_de_Bayonne" title="Jardin botanique de Bayonne">botanic gardens</a> adjoin the walls on both sides of the Nive.\n</p><p>The area across the Adour is largely residential and industrial, with much demolished to make way for the railway. The Saint-Esprit church was part of a bigger complex built by <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI_of_France" title="Louis XI of France">Louis&#160;XI</a> to care for <a href="/wiki/Way_of_St_James" class="mw-redirect" title="Way of St James">pilgrims to Santiago de Compostela</a>. It is home to a wooden <i>Flight into Egypt</i> sculpture.\n</p><p>Overlooking the quarter is Vauban\'s 1680 Citadelle. The soldiers of Wellington\'s army who died besieging the citadelle in 1813 are buried in the nearby English Cemetery, visited by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> and other British dignitaries when staying in <a href="/wiki/Biarritz" title="Biarritz">Biarritz</a>.\n</p><p>The distillery of the famous local liqueur <a href="/wiki/Izarra_(liqueur)" title="Izarra (liqueur)">Izarra</a> is located on the northern bank of the Adour and is open to visitors.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Caserne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bayonne_Caserne.jpg/220px-Bayonne_Caserne.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bayonne_Caserne.jpg/330px-Bayonne_Caserne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Bayonne_Caserne.jpg/440px-Bayonne_Caserne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bayonne_Caserne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Citadel</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personalities">Personalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Personalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Edmund_Crouchback" title="Edmund Crouchback">Edmund Crouchback</a> or Edmond Plantagenet, <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Lancaster" title="Earl of Lancaster">Earl of Lancaster</a>, born in 1245 at <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and died in 1296 at Bayonne, was an English prince. Second surviving son of King <a href="/wiki/Henri_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Henri III">Henri III</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Provence" title="Eleanor of Provence">Eleanor of Provence</a>, he was the 1st Earl of Lancaster and the founder of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lancaster" title="House of Lancaster">House of Lancaster</a>;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jean_du_Vergier_de_Hauranne" title="Jean du Vergier de Hauranne">Jean du Vergier de Hauranne</a>, (1581\xe2\x80\x931643), <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theologian</a>, who introduced <a href="/wiki/Jansenism" title="Jansenism">Jansenism</a> into France</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guillaume_du_Tillot" title="Guillaume du Tillot">Guillaume du Tillot</a> (1711\xe2\x80\x931774), politician</li>\n<li>Marguerite Brunet, called <a href="/wiki/Mademoiselle_Montansier" title="Mademoiselle Montansier">Mademoiselle Montansier</a>, born in 1730 at Bayonne and died in 1820 at Paris, was an actress and director of theatre. The house where she was born still exists in Rue des Faures, at Bayonne;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dominique_Joseph_Garat" title="Dominique Joseph Garat">Dominique Joseph Garat</a> (1749\xe2\x80\x931833), writer and politician</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Cabarrus" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Cabarrus">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Cabarrus</a> (1752\xe2\x80\x931810), French adventurer and Spanish financier</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Armand_Joseph_Dubernad" title="Armand Joseph Dubernad">Armand Joseph Dubernad</a> (1741\xe2\x80\x931799), financial trader, <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)#Consul_general" title="Consul (representative)">consul general</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Pelletier" title="Bertrand Pelletier">Bertrand Pelletier</a> (1761\xe2\x80\x931797), chemist and pharmacologist</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Laffitte" title="Jacques Laffitte">Jacques Laffitte</a> (1767\xe2\x80\x931844), banker and politician</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Bastiat" title="Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Bastiat">Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric Bastiat</a> (1801\xe2\x80\x931850), <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical-liberal</a> author and <a href="/wiki/Political_economy" title="Political economy">political economist</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Lavigerie" title="Charles Lavigerie">Charles Lavigerie</a> born at Bayonne in 1825 and died in 1892 at <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> (Alg\xc3\xa9rie), was a 19th-century Cardinal. He was the founder of the <i>Society of Missionaries of Africa</i> which is better known under the name <a href="/wiki/White_Fathers" title="White Fathers">White Fathers</a>;</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Bonnat" title="L\xc3\xa9on Bonnat">L\xc3\xa9on Bonnat</a> (1833\xe2\x80\x931922), painter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Altarriba_y_Villanueva" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Altarriba y Villanueva">Ram\xc3\xb3n Altarriba y Villanueva</a> (1841\xe2\x80\x931906), Spanish Carlist politician</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Cassin" title="Ren\xc3\xa9 Cassin">Ren\xc3\xa9 Cassin</a> (1887\xe2\x80\x931976), lawyer and judge; recipient of the 1968 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Duhourcau" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Duhourcau">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Duhourcau</a> (1883\xe2\x80\x931851), writer and historian</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Michel_Camdessus" title="Michel Camdessus">Michel Camdessus</a> (born 1933), managing director of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> from 1997 to 2000</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Didier_Deschamps" title="Didier Deschamps">Didier Deschamps</a> (born 1968), <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World-Cup</a>-winning footballer</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Imanol_Harinordoquy" title="Imanol Harinordoquy">Imanol Harinordoquy</a> (born 1980), <a href="/wiki/France_national_rugby_union_team" title="France national rugby union team">French international</a> rugby union player</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Dupuis" class="mw-redirect" title="Anthony Dupuis">Anthony Dupuis</a> (born 1973), professional tennis player</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sylvain_Luc" title="Sylvain Luc">Sylvain Luc</a> (born 1965), <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> guitarist</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Xavier_de_le_Rue" class="mw-redirect" title="Xavier de le Rue">Xavier de le Rue</a> (born 1979), a <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarder</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Joe_Duplantier" title="Joe painter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Ruffier" title="St\xc3\xa9phane Ruffier">St\xc3\xa9phane Ruffier</a> (born 1986) a <a href="/wiki/French_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" Laporte">Aymeric Laporte</a>, footballer. Raised in the city.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bayonne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>In <a href="/wiki/Wyndham_Lewis" title="Wyndham Lewis">Wyndham Lewis</a>\'s novel <i>The Wild Body</i> (1927) the protagonist, Ker-Orr, in the first story, "A Soldier of Humour", takes the train from Paris and stays in Bayonne before going to Spain.</li>\n<li>In <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_Also_Rises" title="The Sun Also Rises">The Sun Also Rises</a></i>, three of the characters visit Bayonne en route to <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>, Spain.</li>\n<li>In <a href="/wiki/Kim_Stanley_Robinson" title="Kim Stanley Robinson">Kim Stanley Robinson</a>\'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Years_of_Rice_and_Salt" title="The Years of Rice and Salt">The Years of Rice and Salt</a></i> (2002), Bayonne is the first city recolonized by the Muslims after the total depopulation of Europe by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>. Named "Baraka", its earliest colonizers were later driven out by rivals from <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a> and flee to the <a href="/wiki/Loire_Valley" title="Loire Valley">Loire Valley</a>, where they found the city of Nsara.</li>\n<li>In <a href="/wiki/Trevanian" title="Trevanian">Trevanian</a>\'s novel <a href="/wiki/Shibumi_(novel)" title="Shibumi (novel)">Shibumi</a>, Hannah has been called as "a whore from Bayonne" by elderly <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basque</a> women in a village of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Basque_Country" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Basque Country">Northern Basque Country</a>.</li>\n<li>The seventh track of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Bonamassa" title="Joe Bonamassa">Joe Bonamassa</a>\'s album <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl_(album)" title="Dust Bowl (album)">Dust Bowl</a> is entitled <i>The Last Matador of Bayonne</i>.</li>\n<li>In the summer of 2008, <a href="/wiki/Manu_Chao" title="Manu Chao">Manu Chao</a>\'s live album <i><a href="/wiki/Baionarena" class="mw-redirect" title="Baionarena">Baionarena</a></i> was recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Amphitheatre" title="Amphitheatre">Arena</a> of Bayonne.</li>\n<li>The album <a href="/wiki/Life_is_Elsewhere" title="Life is Elsewhere">Life is Elsewhere</a>, by English band <a href="/wiki/Little_Comets" title="Little Comets">Little Comets</a>, features a song titled Bayonne.,</li>\n<li>The eighth track of La Nef\'s album <i>La Traverse Miraculeuse</i> is entitled <i>Le Navire de Bayonne</i>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" still visible in parts was in the shape of a polygon of 1,125 metres (3,691 feet) perimeter in an area of 6&#160;to 9 hectares (15\xe2\x80\x9322 acres).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Andelot" title="Treaty of Andelot">Treaty of Andelot</a> signed in 587 between <a href="/wiki/Guntram" title="Guntram">Guntram</a>, king of Burgundy, and <a href="/wiki/Brunhilda_of_Austrasia" title="Brunhilda of Austrasia">Brunhilda of Austrasia</a>, mentions Lapurdo; it documents the return to Brunhilda of several cities including Aire, Couserans and <i>Lapurdo</i>, each "with its territories" ("cum terminibus"). Manex Goyhenetche indicates that in the 6th century, the term <i>civitas</i> was used to designate a fortress. "The <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> dynasties of Austrasia and Neustria by the Treaty of Andelot, consolidated their grip on part of the former territory of the <i>Nine Peoples</i> [...] In the 4th century Lapurdum continued to exist and by the end of the 6th century returned to its function as a fortress. Lapurdum controlled firstly the routes leading to the Pyrenean passes and secondly the <a href="/wiki/Cabotage" title="Cabotage">cabotage</a> routes of the Frankish fleets from <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">Bordeaux</a> to <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a> ".</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Vicount resided in Chatelet (<i>lou Castet</i>), next to the entry to the current <i>Cinq Cantons</i> (Five Cantons) which was the Roman gate leading to the port (source: Eugene Goyheneche, <i>The Basque Country: Soule, Labourd, Lower Navarre</i>, New Society regional editions and distribution, Pau, 1979 (Record BNF FRBNF34647711).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It can be deduced that it existed prior to that date.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Relations with Labourd were often difficult and caused many bloody conflicts. The most famous of them took place in 1343 when the mayor of Bayonne, P\xc3\xa9 de Poyane, killed five labourdin nobles: an episode which, according to Eugene Goyheneche, had its origin in a fictional story of <i>On the Proudines bridge</i> at <a href="/wiki/Villefranque,_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Atlantiques" title="Villefranque, Pyr\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9es-Atlantiques">Villefranque</a>, retold by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Augustine_Chaho&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Augustine Chaho (page does not exist)">Augustine Chaho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hippolyte_Taine" title="Hippolyte Taine">Hippolyte Taine</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example a Bayonnais fleet participated in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Calais_(1346)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Calais (1346)">Siege of Calais</a> led by the English in 1346 which consisted of 15 vessels and 439 men (source: Eugene Goyheneche, The Basque Country: Soule, Labourd, Lower Navarre, Society new regional editions and distribution, Pau,1979 (Record BNF FRBNF34647711), p. 163. <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-79">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The siege lasted nine days from 12 to 20 August 1451 according to Pierre Hourmat, <i>History of Bayonne origins to the French Revolution of 1789</i>, Society of Arts Science &amp; Arts of Bayonne,1986, p. 143.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Two annual fairs: one on the first day of Lent and the other the 1st August: "[...] grant them free fairs in perpetuity of all Aydes, imposicions, impostz and any other subsidies qualxconques, which one will be held the first day of karesme and the other on the first day of August [...]" as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=4-ZZAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA469">letters patent of Louis XI</a> established at <a href="/wiki/Montferrand,_Puy-de-D%C3%B4me" class="mw-redirect" title="Montferrand, Puy-de-D\xc3\xb4me">Montferrand</a> in May 1462.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Francis I was replaced as a captive by his two eldest sons: <a href="/wiki/Francis_III,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Francis III, Duke of Brittany">Francis III, Duke of Brittany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a> who were finally released in 1530 after payment of the ransom.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The second <a href="/wiki/Gare_de_Bayonne" title="Gare de Bayonne">Gare de Bayonne</a> succeeded an earlier station made of wood and metal built in 1854 at the beginning of the 20th century</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Forges of the Adour were actually located in the commune of <a href="/wiki/Boucau" title="Boucau">Boucau</a> on the right bank of the river.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It was in these terms that the newspaper <i>Le Courrier de Bayonne</i> recounted the event a few days later.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i>Courrier de Bayonne</i> of 8 August 1914 described the departure of the Regiment in the following terms: "[...] As for the trains which carried our brave little poilus of the 49th, they were adorned with flowers. On the wagons were pleasant or patriotic inscriptions. We noted the following: "Pleasure Train for Berlin, out and back"; on others: "Vive la France! Long live England&#160;! Long live Russia&#160;!" were framed by garlands and on the locomotives were the flags of the three countries fraternally chattering in the wind ... If the Germans saw it, perhaps they would not be very sure of victory. [...]" (Source: Maurice Sacx, Bayonne and the Basque Country\xe2\x80\x94Witnesses of history, Biarritz, Basque Museum of Bayonne, 1968).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-115">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Avenue of the Czech Legion in Bayonne is in their honour.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Polish company was cited in an order of the Army dated 21 June 1918, by <a href="/wiki/General_Petain" class="mw-redirect" title="General Petain">General Petain</a> (source: Fran\xc3\xa7ois Lafitte Houssat, Bayonne Nive and Adour, Joue-les-Tours, Alan Sutton, 2001 (<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/2-84253-557-X" title="Special:BookSources/2-84253-557-X">2-84253-557-X</a>)).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-121">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The shooting took place at the Saint-L\xc3\xa9on crossroads near the train station and near the citadel.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-123">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This blazon was effective 3 August 1919, by the municipal council of the city of Bayonne, quoted by Ren\xc3\xa9 Broca in the preface of the book <i>History of Bayonne from its origins to the French Revolution of 1789</i>, Pierre Hourmat, Corporation Sciences Humanities &amp; Arts, Bayonne, 1986</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Ch\xc3\xa2teau-Neuf was completed in 1507 by Roger de Gramont.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-133"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-133">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">At the beginning of the 21st century, the methods of identification have been modified by <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160306074946/https://www.legifrance.gouv.fr/affichTexte.do?cidTexte=JORFTEXT000000593100">Law No. 2002-276 of 27 February 2002</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160306074946/https://www.legifrance.gouv.fr/affichTexte.do?cidTexte=JORFTEXT000000593100">Archived</a> 6 March 2016 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>., the so-called "law of local democracy" and in particular Title V "census operations" allows, after a transitional period running from 2004 to 2008, the annual publication of the legal population of the different French administrative districts. For communes with a population greater than 10,000 inhabitants, a sample survey is conducted annually and the entire territory of these communes is taken into account at the end of the period of five years. The first "legal population" after 1999 under this new law came into force on 1 January 2009 and was based on the census of 2006.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-136"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-136">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2014 the Ham Festival was held from 17 to 20 April</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Bayonne Celebrations traditionally begin on the Wednesday preceding the first weekend of August but the schedule has been changed and the start of celebrations has been advanced in recent years because the crowds become too large. They end the following Sunday.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There are 20 sports sections including the <i>Aviron Bayonnais pro rugby</i> and Aviron Bayonnais FC according to the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aviron-bayonnais.asso.fr">Aviron Bayonnais FC website</a> (accessed 29 July 2014).</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-154"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-154">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These remarks are not the result of a statistical study of the data presented; they are only indicative.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Part of the commune is part of the town is in the <a href="/wiki/Appellation_d%27origine_controlee" class="mw-redirect" title="Appellation d&#39;origine controlee">appellation d\'origine controlee</a> (AOC) zone of <a href="/wiki/Ossau-Iraty" title="Ossau-Iraty">Ossau-Iraty</a> but there were no producers in 2014.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h3><span 1789</i>, Society of Sciences Letters Arts of Bayonne,1986, P. 27 to 35 <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span>)deplores the lack of sources for the period 5th century to the 10th century: "If the existence of a major military site is attested by the remains of the tower walls of a castrum, the headquarters or refuge of a cohort in the last days of the Roman Empire, in the half a millennium that followed the collapse of the latter plunges us into an almost total ignorance of who occupied the area of the castrum and the identity of the people. A heavy silence covers the fate of Lapurdum and documents at our disposal for five centuries can be counted on the fingers of one hand and these lead to different or contradictory interpretations ... . So this story becomes a long series of question marks, for example that of Novempopulania".</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Manex Goyhenetche, General History of Basque country, Prehistory, Roman era, Middle Ages<i>, Vol. 1, Elkarlanean, Donostia and Bayonne, 1998, 492 pages, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/2-913156-20-7" title="Special:BookSources/2-913156-20-7">2-913156-20-7</a>, BnF FRBNF37031711, p. 134 <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span>.</i></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On 12 April 1215 <a href="/wiki/John,_King_of_England" title="John, King of England">John, King of England</a>, granted Bayonne a legal personality that would last throughout the Middle Ages and, to some extent, until the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. The form of the charter resembled that of <a href="/wiki/La_Rochelle" title="La Rochelle">La Rochelle</a>. According to Eugene Goyheneche, "the city is governed by the "Hundred Peers" who were actually a mayor, twelve deputies, twelve councilors, and seventy-five peers who were co-opted and proposed each year by the mayor for the king\'s choice. The mayor was head of the administrative, judiciary, and military: he had custody of the keys to the city and some mayors were admirals in the bayonnaise fleet. The king was represented by a marshal" (source: Eugene Goyheneche, The Basque Country: Soule, Labourd, Lower Navarre, Societe new regional editions and distribution, Pau,1979 (Record BNF FRBNF34647711) <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">L\xc3\xa9on Cadier, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://1886.u-bordeaux3.fr/items/show/9538"><i> Seneschal of Lannes under Charles VII, royal administration and provincials states</i></a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since October 2016">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup>, A.
